“You? What about me?”

“Us. You hurt us.”

“Better.”

“Hush you.” Turning aside from their bickering, the twin—Fred maybe?—brought up his wand to the very short fuze. “You’d think you would have learned by now that nothing can stop us.”

A small flame emerged from the tip of the wand, lighting the fuze as the twins pushed the bomb over the edge.

Hannah threw herself on top of Astoria while Millicent dove behind a tree for cover. Raising his wand high, Neville materialized a glimmering shield in mid-air, only for the bombe to pass right through it, falling unimpaired toward them as the fuze ran out.

Neville shut his eyes and shielded his head with his arms moments before the laugh of the twins and the loud explosion was heard ... but not felt.

“Hmm ... Not enough sugar I think.”

“I told you! And it’s not solid enough. You were too heavy-handed with the milk.”

He opened his eyes, expecting to see his garden ravaged and greenhouses devastated, only to see the ground covered in thick white cream. Standing in the middle of the white sea that had somehow spared everything and everyone else, the twins were tasting the cream as if nothing was amiss.

“Guys ... What the hell?”

“Ah! Back with us?”

“What do you think Nev? Is it good?”

“I don’t...” He looked down at his clothes, finding no trace of the cream. He looked back at the twins, bewildered. “What is this?”

“A bit slow, innit?” One of the twins—he was pretty sure this was George now—took a handful of cream off the floor and offered it to him. “Why don’t you have a taste?”

With an uncertain hand, Neville tried to take a piece, only for his hand to pass right through George’s, which became a multicoloured blur for an instant before reforming itself, prompting another laughing fit.

Looking around once more, making sure that nothing had been damaged and taking in the absurdity of the situation, Neville finally let himself relax and joined in their laughter while the others got back up.

“Your plants are fine. Nothing to fear.”

“We’ve found this nifty little program and we just had to try it out.”

“Holograms! What do you think?”

“Bloody confusing, that’s what. So you aren’t really here?”

“Nope!”

“We’re in the main storage room right now.”

“In hindsight, not the best place to detonate a cream bomb. Everything is covered in it now.”

“Alright, I admit, this was good.” Neville pocketed his wand, a large grin on his face as he tried to repress another laugh. “Though you really should have tied it from further away.”

“Please, who do you take us for? This is nothing.”

“This thing has a range of thousands of kilometres.”

“We already managed to surprise Lee back in Diagon when Requirement was in orbit yesterday.”

“Not what I meant.”

In the corner of his eye, he could see Astoria drying her tears in Millicent’s robes while Hanna opened the door, wand in hand and fury in her eyes.

“Weasleys!”

“If I were you, I wouldn’t have done it from the next room over.”

The twins looked at each other in terror before turning tails. They tried to run for a door only they saw, but slipped in the cream and fell head-first in it before their projections disappeared, returning the garden to its pristine glory.

“So, girls.” Neville turned toward them with his most reassuring smile. “Want to see what we’ve been working on lately?

Like a Roller-coaster

“Come on. You can do it.”

Lee’s encouragement might have been heartwarming in another situation, but they only served to distract Hermione while she was focusing with all of her will not to look down.

Or up.

Or anywhere except toward the Requirement’s stern which grew ever closer as she hobbled forward on her hoverboard.

This ship was way too big and any wrong move would send her to drift into the void where she would die and oh god why had she agreed to do this it’s mad and only a mad person would agree to it this wasn’t safe by any definition of the word.

Just because she had designed the thing did not mean she had to be the one to install it, right? Same as the hoverboards. Sure, she had been the one to design them, but it didn’t mean she liked using one to float in deep space with it!

The absence of gravity was not exactly helping, and her hands hurt from grasping the safety cable she had insisted on using, knowing that her life could very well depend on it.

“Everything alright out here?”

Bridget sounded impatient.

Had she already been outside long enough for that? Was she too slow?

She knew she could not have left the airlock more than a few minutes ago, but she did not dare to look behind to see how far she had come. She was torn between taking as long as she would need to do this as safely as she could and rushing to end it as soon as possible.

“Yeah, we’re almost there. Come on Hermione, just a bit further... Here.”

As fast as she could, Hermione let go of the cable with one hand to grasp at the one Lee was holding out for her. With his help, she stepped off the hoverboard and set foot on the ship’s hull, the magnetic lock of her boots engaging when Lee pressed one of the buttons on her left vambrace.

“Thanks.”

“No problem.” Despite the full face plating of his helmet, she could hear the smile in his voice. The clear visors had disappeared from the new deep space suits they were wearing, one of the many changes along a much thicker undersuit and reinforced plating that limited their range movements in exchange for the added protection. “We’re in position. You can conjure the first module.”

“Alright, here it comes.”

Bridget moved a command stone on her console and a flash of white light engulfed the screen behind it, disappearing shortly after to once again display a view of the rear side of the ship. In it, their two space-bound “astronauts” were already busing themselves, waving wands and tools around the large armoured pod she had conjured for them.

“How long will it take to install the modules?”

She was so focused on watching the work of the two people she still had trouble calling her superior officers—Merlin did that sound weird. They were all kids, not soldiers!—that Potter’s question startled her. He had been so quiet since he had come in a few minutes ago, barely acknowledging her presence with a greeting before returning to whatever he was reading on his data-slate, that she had almost forgotten he was here.

“We hope to attach half of the pods today and the rest tomorrow. Once we’re sure they’re holding we’ll have to install the capacitors and link them to the ship’s ... power grid?” Despite being more used to muggle terms than most of her housemates, the sheer amount of information the other engineers had tried to cram into her head these last weeks would have made a N.E.W.T. student-run for the hills. “That should take the better parts of the next two weeks. We’ll still need to run some tests, but after that, we’ll be ready to go.”

“And we’re sure this will work? I don’t want to get everyone’s hopes up only for the engines to blow up when we turn them on.”

“Everything has so far in the simulations. Boot has come up with a proper testing protocol so we can avoid anything like that after the explosion last month.”

Or at least that’s what she’d been told. At the time her most pressing concern had been her exams and not modifying a millennia-old alien spaceship.

Still, she was nothing if not a fast learner and on top of studying Maths and Physics, she had quickly gotten up to speed with most of the projects her team had been working on.

As of late, most of their efforts had been focused on solving the energy generation problem that prevented the ship from travelling to other star systems, something she was still trying to wrap her head around. While the ship had been designed to not only do so but also to travel between galaxies, the very same thing that had allowed Potter and his friends to find it was also what stopped them from doing it themselves. 

The ship had expended its reserves of the elements required to fuel the main reactors, stranding it in their system, and the replacement they had cobbled together was so much less powerful that it was not even funny. Even less so when the hyperdrive, which allowed the ship to travel through an alternate dimension called subspace where they could reach faster-than-light speeds relative to their own dimension—as if all of this wasn’t insane enough already—required prodigious amounts of energy to function.

Several options had been considered, including the cannibalization of other systems which used said elements so that they could power the main reactor. While the idea would have most likely worked, they would have had no way to repair these systems and the fuel would have been consumed in the first jump, leaving them stranded far from Earth if they did not find another source at their destination. Needless to say, this idea had not gathered much support among the crew.

As such, the engineers had to find a solution that would only use the available resources, of which they had more than they could need thanks to the station mining them out of Neptune, and were common enough to be found in any system they could visit.

The idea they had gone with, while neither energy-efficient nor elegant, was to increase their energy production simply by adding more fusion reactors to the ship. After several prototypes, they were now installing them in semi-detached armoured modules on the hull, well within range of the ship’s conjurator array, allowing for their automatic refuelling without reducing too much of the ship’s storage space that would be used to store said fuel.

Their attempts at redesigning the reactor to fit in the modules had been a learning experience on the tensile strength of certain metals and the retrieval of exploded debris floating away in space, but everything had worked out in the end.

With half a dozen of these new reactors attached to the ship, along with massive supercapacitors to store the excess energy, they would be able to accumulate power over time to compensate for huge and punctual power drains like the opening of a hyperspace window.

This solution still came with its limitations, though, as replenishing the reserves took time and their fuel supplies would deplete themselves far quicker than their current rate. While they would not be able to jump between two galaxies, they had estimated their maximum jumping capabilities to be in the hundreds of light years. This was more than enough for them to go out and explore the galaxy in search of the materials required to change to a more efficient system.

“Good. I know the twins aren’t happy with all the new regulations, but we already came close to disaster several times and enough is enough.”

“You know, when you say it like that I think I’m glad we joined up so late.” Bridget rotated the command stone on the console, bringing up another angle of the ship’s stern to follow Lee and Hermione’s work. “With everything I’ve heard, it’s a miracle you didn’t blow yourself up months ago.”

“Yes well, we learned quickly after the first few accidents.”

When Potter moved closer to watch the screen, Bridget got a glimpse of his data-slate. Names, addresses, pictures ... tens of them maybe. All of them were adults and marked with a green rune. Recruiting outside the castle maybe? Or listing You-Know-Who’s people?

Was she even allowed to ask what it was, or was it one of those things they still kept from them? She knew more about the ship and it’s inner-workings than almost everyone outside the engineering team and yet they still refused to talk about their part in the war. Though now that she knew just what they had been doing, she could understand their caution ... not that she didn't find it infuriating.

“Anyway, things seem to be going well.” Potter turned and walked away disinterestedly, putting down his data-slate on the main console before leaving. “Call me if anything comes up.”

And just like that, she was left alone on the bridge. Which, seriously, what the hell?

Couldn’t they either treat them like dangerous guests and guard them at all times or trust them completely? This weird middle ground where they enforced restrictions and yet gave them complete access to their systems was almost insulting.

Bridget was fuming as she picked up a second command stone and placed it on the console brusquely, conjuring a new batch of equipment for the team outside. She turned away from the screen, looking at the forgotten data-slate as if its very presence was offending. Morgana’s tits, she only had to walk up to it and she could access all the sensitive information they were keeping from her if she wanted to. Or use the main console to lock down the ship and take it for herself or whatever. 

Were they really this careless?

She shook her head and went back to work, muttering under her breath about children playing with things they shouldn’t and half-assed security.

Walking down a nearby corridor, Harry had procured another data-slate and was intently watching the surveillance feed of the bridge where an irate girl shook her head and focused back on the secondary console in front of her.

As he put the slate away, a proud smile tugged at his lips.

The stale air of the caves rushed through Harry’s hair as he pulled on yet another lever on the infernal contraption’s control panel. Racing on the hanging high rails, the cart rotated on its axis as it abruptly changed course.

Behind him, somehow maintaining his balance as he stood on the passenger seats, Dumbledore was sending spell after spell at their pursuers. Despite the Headmaster’s swift wand, it seemed like every time one of the carts full of Death Eaters pursuing them toppled over into the abyss, two more emerged from side tunnels, hoping to cut them off.

Harry ducked when he saw a flash of green in the corner of his eye, swearing when it exploded against the ceiling, sending one of the giant stalactites crashing down on the rails. Pushing the main lever to the left with all his strength, Harry managed to force the cart to turn once more, sending them into a side tunnel.

As they plunged ever deeper into the Earth, he could only hope that another down the line would allow them to come back up. Though knowing his luck, things were never that simple. The shouts and grinding of wheels on rails growing closer behind them at least made him sure of it.

And to think that this evening had begun so well.

After numerous inquiries and some unusually forthcoming Goblins, Dumbledore had managed to track down the second to last Horcrux, Hufflepuff’s cup. The bankers were not quite exactly thrilled at the idea of letting them steal it from one of their vaults, however, and had only agreed to it for a price.

Surprising no one, it seemed like the little buggers had a peculiar view on ownership. Especially when dealing with their craftsmen’s work. In addition to a sizable sum, they had demanded the restitution of Gryffindor’s sword.

Which, seeing as it was their only safe way of destroying the Horcruxes, was problematic, to say the least.

The Goblins had been uncompromising at first and only agreed after many concessions and the re-negotiation of their deal with them. He could still hear Justin’s complaints as he tore his own work to shreds for reasons Harry was not ready to share.

While suspicious of their turnabout, a grateful Dumbledore was allowed to buy a new lease on the sword, one that would allow him to keep it until the time of his death, at which point it would be returned to the family of the original craftsman.

With the Goblins’ approval, Harry accompanied Dumbledore through the depths of the bank after business hours in search of the vaults of Voldemort’s inner circle. After repeatedly digging around piles of gold and outdated jewellery, they finally found and destroyed the small golden cup inside the Lestrange vault.

It still seemed strange that such an unassuming thing could house the soul of a psychotic madman.

Of course, things could not go according to plan. They had not even left the vault when a whole slew of Death Eaters had come bearing down on them. Maybe the vault had been protected by wards and enchantments that even the Goblins had not known about, or maybe they had decided that they did not want to wait to reclaim their sword. Either way, Harry and Dumbledore had forced their way out of the vault, past the warm corpse of the dragon and onto one of the carts, turning the trap into a chase as the Death Eaters rained down curses upon them.

While piloting a mine cart held together by wishes and magic through dark tunnels and fighting off a dozen dark wizards did not leave one with much time to ponder on their situation, two things had become clear. 

For one, their little Horcrux hunt was no longer a secret from Voldemort. This would be quite a large problem If they lived through this.

For another, the Goblins would be pissed. He could hear the spells crashing down on Dumbledore’s shields before the tunnel’s walls exploded, showering them with debris.

Not for the first time that night, Harryt cursed himself for leaving his suit and helmet back on the ship, secrecy be damned.

They came out of the tunnel before the Death Eaters managed to bury them, emerging in a wide circular cavern supported by pillars as thick as houses. In its centre, a building that resembled a Roman coliseum rose toward the faraway ceiling, its countless archways housing the fortified doors of vaults as impressive as the Lestrange’s. The sight of another chained dragon resting in what would have been the arena, right by the only rails he could see going back up made him sigh.

How was this his life?

“Hang on tight professor!”

Holding the main lever with a firm hand, Harry waved his wand in a complex pattern in front of him with the other.

 ”Sulatatud Raud!”

A jet of silver light hit the next fork in the rails and the sound of bending metal echoed in the cavern as the rails forcefully switched paths and fused themselves. Bellow them, the dragon opened its blind eyes and raised his horned head toward them to watch as the cart began its mad descent toward the coliseum.

“Harry?”

“Just hang on!”

Spells rained down all around them, crashing on Dumbledore’s shield and the surrounding vaults as the other carts forcefully joined them on the descending track, further agitating the dragon. The beast spread its wings, rising from the ornate stone floor and roared its discontent for all to hear while miss-aimed curses splashed harmlessly on its hide.

Struggling to keep his hold on the controls as their speed and the destruction around them shook the cart, threatening to throw them off-rails, Harry pushed them even further. The cart’s frame groaned under them as it lurched forward, further accelerating their descent. The wheels sent sparks as they raced down the rails at a speed Harry was more accustomed to reaching on a broom, sending them right in the direction of the irate dragon.

“Harry!”

All traces of confusion had left Dumbledore’s voice, leaving only the urgent shrill of panic shared by the shouts of their pursuers.

“Hang. On.” Harry managed to say through teeth gritted so hard they might break.

Their cart shot through the coliseum and broke a wooden barrier as they passed through the station without stopping. With their speed, they crossed most of the coliseum in seconds, the silhouette of the dragon growing closer and more imposing with each of them.

Locking them in place with a foot, Harry finally released his grip on the controls and got up in his seat before turning to face their pursuers. His eyes met Dumbledore’s fearful ones for an instant, leaving his silent question unanswered as he focused on the rails behind them. He raised his wand in jagged movements, fighting against the wind hitting him and ignoring the cold sweat running down his back as he thought back to the time when a blond-haired boy had taught him this spell.

“Maceria Lapidea!”

Behind them, the floor beneath the track exploded when a massive lump of rock emerged from the ground, showering the arena with dust and debris. The cavern echoed the dragon’s roar and the cries of the Death Eaters as they crashed upon it, drowning even Harry’s whoop.

“Get down!”

Dumbledore’s shout was his only warning, and only months of training allowed him to throw himself back in his seat in time, wincing as he hit his shoulder on the control panel. Sprawled on the metal chair, he saw an enormous scaled paw with claws the size of his arm whip the air above him before their speed carried them to a safe distance.

“Are you alright?”

“I’ll live.” He pushed himself back up onto the seat, his shoulder throbbing in disapproval. “Now let’s get out of here.”

He took hold of the commands once more and they lurched forward, picking up their dwindling speed as they climbed out of the cavern, leaving it in chaos as the remaining Death Eaters tried to flee the enraged dragon on foot.

When they finally made it back to the surface, he chanced a look behind them, finding no other cart climbing the slope of the main tunnel.

“Well. That could have gone worse.”

The look Dumbledore gave him was only matched by the ridiculous state of his windswept hair and beard. After a moment, the corner of his mouth twitched and a familiar twinkle shone behind his spectacles.

“Yes. I suppose it could have.”

Somewhere on the coast of Great Britain, a figure draped in billowing dark robes slashed the air with their wand, vanishing the rock face to reveal the gaping mouth of a cave.

Walking at a furious pace, they crossed the threshold and ventured into the darkness with a confidence born of familiarity.

When they reached the shores of a great black lake so large one could not discern the distant banks, their pace did not falter as they rose into the air, flying unimpaired to a barren island.

When a hand as pale as death itself plunged into the green waters of the stone basin, pulling out an ornate locket by its chain, time seemed to stand still.

A serpentine hiss was met with silence and two eyes squinted, their blood-red irises filled with far too familiar emotions.

Long and delicate fingers took hold of the heavy locket, bringing the light to reflect on its many crystal facets where no initial inlaid in green stone could be seen.

The shout fuelled by rage, grief and fear echoed in the cavernous chamber when Lord Voldemort threw the offensive fake into the lake.

Far to the north, Harry Potter was making his way back to the seventh floor, holding his head as a painful ache he had not felt in a long time raged behind his scar.

“Hello, Ms Edgecomb.”

The twenty-year-old Private entered the store, announced by the greeting of the doormat—"Boldly come!"—as Clarissa Edgecomb came out of the office, her arms full of parchment rolls.

“Good morning Toby. Are you alright?”

“Hardly slept a wink.” While his tired features were apparent, it did not stop him from grinning from ear to ear. “I kept thinking that this is it. We’re finally done.”

“That we are.” Clarissa could not stop the smile on her lips at the thought of completing what had been months of work as she put down the parchments on the counter. “Though you should still take the time to rest. We’ll need you at your best for the next few days”

“I know, I know. But once it’s done I’ll be transferred up there you know? I just can’t wait.” Toby walked up to the counter, taking off his messenger bag and dropping it to the ground. “Is this it?”

“Part of it at least. The rest is still in the back.”

Taking a parchment off the pile, she unrolled it to reveal a list of names, addresses and the roles most suited to their set of skills should they agree to take the job. Despite all the time she had spent vetting the candidates with Toby and Hannah, she could still find a few names that she did not recognize. Those Creevy boys had done a wonderful job getting the American branch of Enterprise up and running and it seems their candidates had made the cut.

“I have a kettle on the stove. I was thinking that we could use a cuppa before writing all these letters. Would you mind taking care of it while I prepare things here?”

“Ms Edgecomb, you’re a saint. I’ll go get it.”

Toby disappeared in the back of the store, to the small rec room they shared with the Granger’s practice. After checking that the sign on the front door was still announcing the store as closed, Clarissa pulled out quills, inkwells and blank parchments from the shelves.

She liked these moments. When the warm rays of the spring sun shined through the storefront and all she could hear were the familiar sounds of the parchment and the distant whistle of the kettle. It was an oasis of peace and simplicity the gloom and folly that had taken over her world.

She knew what was happening out there, and she had heard about how the crew had been helping people. She just did not expect to hear that they had thrown themselves into the fight when they had not even graduated yet!

She had not known Lieutenant MacMillan very well. Mostly, she had only spoken with him to report the happenings of the shop when Lee had been busy with one project or another. Still, to hear that such a sweet boy—just a year younger than Marietta!—had died ... It had been quite a shock.

She just hoped that Marietta would remain safe on the ship and far from all of this violence.

She was reaching for the stacks of envelopes under the counter when she froze, the ground shaking beneath her feet while a deep rumble could be heard in the distance.

“Ms Edgecomb?” Toby called from the back. “Is everything alright?”

“I don’t know...”

Her heart was racing.

She was worrying for nothing. It was probably just Mr Rowland trying some new potion recipes down the street again.

The ground shook anew and a few of the parchments fell off the counter. The rumbling was louder and closer this time, and if she strained her ear, she could almost hear voices.

With trembling steps, she approached the storefront, ignoring Toby’s calls as she saw people fleeing down the street.

Her blood turned cold when she saw them.

Half a dozen figures, draped in dark robes and hidden behind masks, throwing spells at stores and people alike.

Death Eaters. Out in the open.

“Toby! We have to-”

The glare of the sun reflected on a polished silver mask was the last thing she saw before a wand sliced through the air and the storefront exploded before her.

Fires of War

Shards of wood and glass filled the air, the remnants of the storefront tearing through everything in their path.

Fear gave way to shock and shock to pain as Clarissa crashed onto the floor, the arms she had raised to protect her head hanging limply in a growing pool of her blood.

She heard shouts behind her, distant and muffled by a persistent ringing in her ears.

Clarissa could feel herself grow cold as her blood left her, despite the air becoming unbearably hot around her.

With effort, she opened her eyes, and the glare of the flames devouring the aisles around her almost made her close them again. Her eyelids were heavy, yet she knew they would forever remain shut if she allowed them to close.

Through the dark spots in her vision, she could see three dark figures standing on the other side of the gaping hole that had been the storefront, the flames engulfing the shop reflecting on their polished silver masks.

Their wands rose once more, the glow of magic at their tip, and her jumbled thoughts turned to Marietta and the terrifying comfort brought by the prospect of a quick release from her agony.

However, another kind of hope bloomed in her heart when the store shutters came crashing down, hiding the Death Eaters from view.

Muffled cries filled the air once more and she could feel multiple pairs of hands getting a hold of her. She felt herself be pulled back and her body warm up as a trembling wand moved over her.

Toby and the Grangers, trying to save her when death had already staked its claim on her. Of course they were. She was not the one they should be worried about, however.

Already, she could see the gold and silver shutters rattle against their frame, the reinforced metal groaning as it strained against the unseen assault.

“No... Leave me...”

Her broken body had been dragged no further than the counter when she was thrown to the ground once more. Her head hit the floor, sending a new flare of pain and blurring her view of the world that shook all around her.

And yet, she could see them, their black robes standing out against the burning remains of her shop like dark holes in the fabric of the world, advancing inexorably to extinguish their lives.

In a cruel boon, the world stopped turning and the ringing in her ears diminished, bringing into focus the roar of the flames and the trembling face of Toby as he stepped in front of her, wand in hand.

She did not want to see or hear what was to come. She did not want the last thing she saw to be Toby’s death.

“Hey, arseholes! You really so ugly that you need to wear masks to hide your mugs?”

The shout cut through the sombre atmosphere, filled with cocky assurance and anger.

Toby’s legs gave out and revealed the three figures turning their backs on them, their wands raised toward the street where Lee Jordan stood alone, his arms crossed and his face twisted in anger.

“What? Nothing? God, your boss is pants at picking his goons. You don’t even know how to shop without wrecking the place.”

The cold grip of dread grasped Clarissa’s heart.

He should not be here. No one else had to die. Had he brought other children to fight?

Oh Merlin, Marietta...

Nonpulsed by the insults, the Death Eaters moved as one, slashing the air with their wands as vicious green and yellow curses flew toward Lee.

And passed right through him.

“No, really, it’s almost sad to watch. Can’t find good help these days. Though it might have something to do with how you’re trying to kill half of the workforce.”

More spells were flung at him, each leaving him unarmed as they passed through his body to crash on the boarded-up storefront behind him to the growing irritation of their casters.

“What trickery is this?”

“The distracting kind.”

Appearing out of thin air behind them, three teenagers in familiar suits—two in green and silver and one in blue and bronze—sent a red spell to the unsuspecting Death Eaters’ backs. They collapsed to the ground like puppets whose strings had been cut, the new arrivals breaking their wands as Lee’s image blurred and disappeared.

“Mum!” The blue figure ripped off her helmet, revealing a face Clarissa had thought she would never see again as she rushed to her side. “Mum, I’m so sorry. We took too long and-”

“Marietta...”

“Don’t talk. Oh Merlin, don’t talk.” Her face was stained with tears and twisted in fear. “Don’t worry, we’re getting you out of here.”

Spells rushed past Percy as he threw himself into a compartment, landing painfully on top of a passenger’s shoes.

“Terribly sorry for that.” Ignoring the cries of the terrified Muggles, Percy put his glasses back in place as he pulled himself back up. “Just wait a bit longer, we’ll have you out of here in no time.”

“Get the hell out!” One of the passengers, a middle-aged man with a prominent belly, grabbed a briefcase from the overhead luggage rack and bludgeoned Percy with it. “Get out! Get out! Get out!”

Ducking out of harm’s way, Percy walked back into the corridor with a wide horizontal motion of his wand. One of the Death Eaters waiting for him was violently thrown against the wall and slumped to the ground, unconscious.

As Percy ran for the next compartment, Flobert—one of the Order members accompanying him—peeked out of another to throw a few hexes before ducking back into cover.

This dance had been repeating for a while now and it had made their progress through the train far slower than Percy would have hoped. They had barely managed to evacuate the first car before the Death Eaters had found them out and since then they had to fight for each step they took.

Jules and Nance had already paid the ultimate price to free the last three cars, but had taken out their fair share of Death Eaters before they fell. It did not seem to matter, however, as for every dark wizard they fell, two more were waiting for them in the next car.

A cry of pain came from the corridor and Percy once again stepped into the line of fire. Fighting off the tears in his eyes and the bile in his throat, he ran over Terence’s body as it lay in a pool of blood and entrails on the carpeted floor. His blasting curse impacted a shield, blasting away the nearby window but leaving the Death Eater unarmed.

Cursing under his breath, Percy ran for the next compartment and tried the door. It refused to open. Behind its glass half, he could see the terrified faces of a family, looking back at him as they huddled together in a corner.

The unlocking charm was so simple that a first-year at Hogwarts could cast it. It was, however, far too slow. Already, he could see the light of an impending curse in the corner of his eye.

He threw himself to the ground, knowing that it would only make the next curse that much harder to avoid. 

Only one way out now.

“Flobert!” He called out as the curse flew above him. “We’re leaving!”

Lounging forward and twisting his body in mid-air as he got up, Percy pushed the sight of the curse rushing toward him out of his mind and focused all his will on the memory of the Order’s Headquarters.

“For Morgana’s sake, don’t you get tired of getting yourself in these situations?”

His head impacted something hard and Percy fell back to the ground as the curse crashed on a blue-tinted shield not two feet from him. Appearing out of thin air in front of him was a familiar silhouette clad head to toe in gold and red.

“I swear, this is the last time I’m saving your arse.”

The girl raised her second arm in front of her and another shield sprang to life. Curse after curse crashed harmlessly upon her shields as she marched toward the Death Eaters, undeterred. When she reached them, they tried to retreat, only to find the door locked with another armoured figure waving at them from the other side. She made short work of the two men, knocking them out and breaking their wands.

“Not to be ungrateful,” Massaging the growing bump on his head, Percy pulled himself off the ground as Flobert came out of hiding, wand raised. Behind the girl, the car’s door clicked open and two similarly dressed figures walked in. “But who are you people?”

The newcomers did not even spare them a glance as they brought the unconscious Death Eaters’ arms to their back and into pearly white metallic tubes. With the press of a button, the tubes shrunk down, locking them into place like some sort of one-piece handcuffs.

“Reinforcements.” The girl’s shields disappeared with a sharp of her arms. “Now, we gonna stand here all day or you gonna lower the wand and make yourselves useful?”

The sight of his companions lying dead a few feet behind them still fresh in mind, Percy exchanged a look with Flobert before bringing up his own wand.

“We’ll need a bit more than that I’m afraid.”

“Ugh, we don’t have time for this!” With a soft hissing sound, the girl removed her helmet, revealing an all too familiar face framed by cropped ginger hair. “Happy?”

“Ginny?” Percy’s eyes went wide in shock and his wand arm went down faster than Charlie on Mum’s shepherd's pie. “What the hell are you doing here?”

“Saving your arse, that’s what. I should be the one asking you that! Last I heard you were working for those guys.”

In any other situation, Percy might have winced under her withering glare. Today, however...

“Saving my—I’m with the Order! You’re sixteen! You should be in school, not fighting on a bloody train!”

“Oh yes, because those NEWTs are really going to help when the Ministry will have razed the country!”

“Does Mum even know you’re here? Does anybody?” He walked up to her, fuzzing about her in search of any injury. “And those armours. Was it you at the Ministry? You’re gonna get yourself killed!”

“We can handle ourselves.” She looked past him as her gaze fell upon Terence’s remains. “Which is more than I can say for you at the moment.“

Percy did not know what to say. Indignation and concern battled in his throat and tied his tongue as he looked at Ginny. A Ginny so far removed from the little girl she had been when he had left the Burrow, turning his back on his family.

When had she turned so cold and serious? So used to violence and death that she could so callously disregard the death of a good man? Ginny and her friends had been fighting in this war for months now. Was it already too late to save their innocence? The childhood that had been robbed from them?

Could he have stopped it if he had stayed?

“Percy?”

Behind them, Flobert had lowered his wand and was now looking warily at the teenagers while holding his left side. 

“It’s alright. They’re with us.” With a sigh, he turned back to Ginny. “Since you’re here, I assume you already know the Death Eaters have launched simultaneous raids across the entire country.”

“Yeah, we know.” One of Ginny’s companions spoke up. “They’re not exactly being discreet about it either.”

“No, they’re not. We weren’t warned in time to stop them, so we’re mostly doing damage control and getting the Muggles out of here.” A shame most obliviators had been spared by the ideological purge at the Ministry and were still happily working for Malfoy. Even if they managed to stop the raids, the fallout would be disastrous. “We’ve already taken care of the care behind us, but we’ve encountered far more resistance than should be needed to take over the train. They-”

The train lurched forward, throwing them back as it picked up speed and turning the scenery on the other side of the window into a blur of colours.

Steadying himself on the wall of the car, Percy straightened his glasses in time to see Ginny put her strange helmet back on. He did not know whether its smooth metal surface or her glare was the more alien to him.

“Report.”

“We’re picking up serious speed and approaching London.” The third teenager, a girl dressed in bronze and gold, said urgently. “At this rate, it will crash when it arrives in the city.”

”We need to get to the locomotive and pull the break.”

“Hold on.” Percy stepped in as the three already turned toward the door. “They know we’re here. They’ll be waiting for us.”

“Then we split up.” She turned toward her companions. “Take mister ungrateful here and get the muggles off the train.” She glanced at Percy over her shoulder before walking away urgently. ”You’re with me.” 

Percy exchanged one last look with Flobert before hurrying after his sister.

“Since when are you in charge?”

“Since you lost control of the situation.”

They came out of the car and onto the small platforms above the coupling. The air rushing by them made crossing the short distance arduous, each step having to be taken with the support of the grab bars on each side of the doors.

“By fighting while you snuck around! We didn’t have the element of surprise like you did.” His righteous anger and indignation fell on deaf ears as Ginny ignored him in favour of freeing and unfolding the service ladder to the roof. “You’re kidding.”

“Nope.”

“This is insane. Do you have any idea how fast we’re going right now?”

“Unless you know what the locomotive looks like so we can apparate there, it’s the quickest way. My board is too small to carry us both. Now come on. We don’t have much time.”

As Ginny climbed the ladder’s first steps, Percy resigned himself to the madness that had become his life. Grumbling under his breath, he cast a quick sticking charm on his glasses—an unpleasant necessity—and climbed after her. The fact that they held firmly on his nose when the wind hit him with the force of a brick wall at least counterbalanced the gross feeling of the metal frames glueing themselves to his skin.

Percy pushed himself onto the roof and steadied himself with Ginny’s help. Despite the wind and complete lack of anything to support herself, she stood straight in defiance of the elements.

“Mag-boots. Now hold on tight.” As he held on the armoured plates covering her shoulders for dear life, they began their march against the wind. “So, you’re with the Order now?”

“You want to do this now?” He shouted, the sound of his voice somehow reaching her.

“Not like I have any other time to ask.” He could feel her shrug beneath his grip. “You don’t even answer our letters anymore.”

“Yes well, I’ve been busy. And my mail was being watched.” He sighed. This was not the way he had wanted this discussion to happen. His careful plans of a quiet evening at the Burrow after the war shattered and joined the rest of his ambitions in the pile of his broken dreams. “I got in touch with Dad’s friends after Fudge died. I’m not proud it took me so long to see what the Ministry had become, but I’ve been trying to make it right you know?”

For a few moments, his only answer was the howling of the wind. They reached the end of the car and jumped onto the next, giving them a glimpse of the spellfire illuminating the train behind them.

“Does Mum know?”

“I...” More than the wind stopped the words in his throat as they resumed their march. “No. For months I worked anonymously, passing on classified information and warning them of Auror activity to my contact in the Order. When I had to flee, I went into hiding and didn’t see much of anyone for weeks.”

Another car coupling, another jump, and the locomotive was now in sight.

“You could have told us. Ask to meet us at headquarters. Passed along a message through your contact.”

“I know.” The accusation hit him like a punch. Not that he had not expected it. ”I wanted to go. To see her and tell her everything. To explain. But I... I just couldn’t. Not with everything still going on. Not when Dad... is still not back.”

“So you preferred letting us think that you hated us and that you were helping the Ministry. Smart move, that.”

“It’s not that simple! And what about you? Does Mum know you’re running around in that armour, fighting Death Eaters and sneaking into the Ministry? Does Ron?“

Ginny stopped and turned around, grasping his wrist to steady him. Despite the helmet, Percy could feel the burning glare of his sister.

“At least my secret isn’t breaking the heart of my family.”

She let go of him and he fell, scrambling to find something to hold as she climbed down a ladder. Gritting his teeth, Percy pushed against the wind and followed after her.

She was already opening the locomotive’s door when he came down the ladder, throwing herself toward the ambush as curses filled the air once more. She walked down the corridor undeterred, the barrage of spellfire crashed harmlessly on the shields coming out of her forearms until she reached the first compartment. She made quick work of the Death Eater inside, leaving his body to fall floor with those of the murdered Muggles already occupying it before continuing her march.

Whatever Ginny was involved with, at least it had her well protected.

Only twice did she have to dodge, when one hijacker more capable than the rabble leading this attack cast the killing curse.

And yet, he fell like the rest.

Percy covered her advance, cursing the Death Eaters from above her shields and taking out the one who attempted to surprise Ginny by apparating behind her.

“I’d scold you for jumping into danger like that, but I can’t argue with the result.”

The battle had been quick, the last Death Earter deciding to flee when he saw his last comrade fall.

“Now let’s stop this-” Hurrying to the front of the car, Percy opened the door to the driver’s compartment, revealing a gaping hole where the controls were supposed to be, cables and broken metal flailing in the wind. “...train.”

“Merlin’s rotten crotch!” No matter how long it had been, Ginny’s vocabulary remained colourful. “Couldn’t these arseholes be subtle, just once?”

“Language.”

“Soon there won’t be anyone to be offended by it.” Past the fields surrounding them, the grey mass of London was growing on the horizon at an alarming rate. “How is this thing even still working?”

“They must have jinxed the engine. Or maybe the wheels. This train won’t stop until it hits something.”

“It won’t.”

Ginny stepped into the remains of the compartment, her boots clamping down on the metal floor as she raised her wand high against the wind.

“Does Hogwarts teach curse-breaking now?”

“No, but I know a spell that can stop the inertia of the train. I’ll have to fight the jinx, but-.”

Behind them, thunderous cracks filled the corridor, delivering half a dozen black-robed figures with wands in hand. No doubt the one that had slipped away had called for backup.

“Muriel’s wrinkled tits!” Percy closed the door just in time to stop a yellow curse from hitting his head. “Can’t they leave us alone for five minutes?”

“Language!” Was this a touch of mirth he heard in her voice? “We don’t have time to take care of them. Can you hold them off?”

He wanted to say no. To grab her and apparate away, far from this madness and the doom that he could see grow closer on the horizon with each passing moment. They had done all they could, saving lives that would have otherwise been lost. There was no way they could stop this train in time. There was no shame in leaving to fight another day.

And yet, seeing her standing here, defiant against fate and the elements, he knew he could not say it.

She was counting on him, and he would not let his family down again.

“Start casting.”

Closing the door behind him, Percy ran into the corridor, his wand swishing through the air. His hand followed the incantations and flowed into the next with the precision that had once made him a straight Os student.

The fire extinguisher tore itself from the wall and exploded as it intercepted a curse, filling the car with white mist. Blinded, the Death Eaters never saw the trolley that flew toward one of them, its metal frame twisting around the body and squeezing tight as their spells hit the walls behind Percy. From the passenger compartments came the bags and briefcases, pummeling into them and making them trip. 

Before he could finish his next spell, a pale flash of light came out of the mists and struck Percy in the stomach. Percy doubled over in pain, throwing up blood, his insides feeling wrong and far less solid than they should be. The sensation was accentuated by the feeling of the train decelerating, his insides moving around like a potion in a too-thin cauldron.

Gritting his bloodied teeth, Percy propped himself up against the wall and raised his trembling wand in a winding pattern. The Death Eater’s shout was short-lived as the howling wind sucked him and the dissipating mist out of the vanished window, revealing the four remaining.

Extending his arm as far as he could before bringing it back sharply, Percy tore the corridor’s floor into a makeshift wall in front of him. He heard another cry and could only hope that this trick had taken another Death Eater as he slumped to the ground. Percy dragged himself to the door, struggling to go through the motion of the locking charm before he leaned heavily against it.

“Perce?”

He could hear Ginny’s muffled voice through the door.

He tried to reply, his words uselessly choking on blood.

Already, he could see the wall he had raised go down and the Death Eaters advance.

They raised their wands as his own laid uselessly beside him, his strength eluding him.

He never could have that talk with his family.

“Confringo.”

And the world went up in flames.

“Is anyone here? Can you hear me?“

Neville’s shouts were drowned by the crackling of the purple flames licking the ancient walls of the apartment, filling the air with noxious smoke. With a thankful thought to the Weasley twins for the air filters of the suit, Neville ran through the smoke-filled hallway, straining his ear in hope of an answer.

He had arrived with Terry and Angelina not ten minutes ago to discover the outskirts of Manchester going up in flames. An entire district was burning, its inhabitants running in the streets while the firefighters had spread out what little manpower they had to contain the flames. Despite their best efforts, the magical fire was probing tenacious and entire blocs had already been turned to ashes.

When their own attempts at dousing the flames failed, the trio had spread out, apparating from one building to the next in search of survivors. Protected by their suits and flame-freezing charms, they had already managed to evacuate well over a dozen Muggles, yet no respite awaited them.

Neville kicked down a door, jumping away when fire burst out of the apartment from the backdraft, singing his side. The armoured plates of his suit spared him from the worst of it, but he could feel the head through the exposed parts. Whatever those flames were, direct contact seemed ill-advised.

Stepping inside the apartment, he felt the wooden floor shift under his weight. The foundations were already weakening and the building was coming down around him. A quick look over the room revealed a charred corpse and an unconscious man on the ground, a half-burnt beam pinning down the remains of his leg.

Pushing down the sick feeling in his stomach, Neville banished the beam away, freeing the man. Taking him in his arms, Neville palpated his throat, searching for a pulse before the building groaned around him. As quickly as he could, he lifted the man and turned on the spot, apparating away as the ceiling collapsed on them.

Down on the street, Neville put the man down next to the other survivors, exchanging a nod with Angelina before she apparated away with another, taking them to a hospital. Behind him, the six-story building collapsed, unable to support its own weight.

He had not gone past the third floor.

Tightening his grip on his father’s wand, Neville turned on the spot once more, apparating on the other side of a window of the next building, his search starting anew.

The first few apartments only housed the charred remains of trapped families, the right side of the building having collapsed and taken with it the stairs. Men, women, children, pets... the flames had spared none. Fighting the urge to vomit after witnessing the remains of a toddler in the arms of his father buried under bricks and wood, he apparated on the floor above through a hole in the ceiling.

“Anyone still here?” He moved through the floor, going from one ruined apartment to the next. “Shout if you can!”

“Help!” A woman’s voice answered. Distorted and barely discernible through the cacophony of the flames and falling debris, but a voice nonetheless. Someone was alive! “Help me!”

“I’m coming!”

Neville ran through the inferno, breaking the door blocking his path with a wave of his wand and emerged in a large living room. The flames had yet to breach the place, leaving it mostly intact. However, he could already see their glow through the cracks in the walls and floor.

Stanger still, was the absence of the woman who had cried out for him.

A heavy blow in his back threw him to the floor, head first, leaving in his wake the remains of the armour that had taken the hit.

“I thought I heard a little pest running around.“ The same voice. He could hear it clearly this time. Filled with mirth and cruelty. “But I didn’t expect it to be this small.”

Neville pushed himself off the ground and turned around, hatred filling his heart as he recognized the woman facing him.

“Lestrange.”

“Oh? Know enough to see you drew the short wand, do you?” Bellatrix’s predatory smile turned to a frown. “Can’t say the same I’m afraid. Then again, I didn’t expect Dumbledore to actually come to this dump.”

“So this was a trap?” Get her talking. Gain some time to breathe and think. Find an opening. “You killed hundreds of people to lure Dumbledore out of Hogwarts?”

“Aren’t we have a spirited little mouse? Getting angry over some Muggles? You might be fun to play with before I go look elsewhere, after all.”

Her wand was at the ready. He needed to distract her. He couldn’t let her strike first.

“You’re a monster. Always have been.” Neville got up, unlatching his helmet with his free hand. “And you need to be put down.” His helmet fell to the floor with a thud, revealing his face, twisted in rage, his hair sticking to his face with sweat. “I am Neville Longbottom. Son of Frank and Alice. This is where you die.”

She stood there for a moment, looking at him in shock until she roared with laughter.

“The Longbottom kid? Is that the best Dumbledore’s little club can spare nowadays?” Neville stood his ground, wand at the ready. Waiting. Watching. “Oh, this is going to be fun. I always regretted not being able to finish the job, you know? Too bad I couldn’t take care of the old crone myself.”

Neville’s grip on his father’s wand was strong enough that a small part of him feared it might snap. It did not matter, however, as the rest was too busy seeing red.

Red and purple.

“Accio, you bitch.”

Wooden debris engulfed in purple flames flew through the open door and toward Bellatrix’s back.

“Tsk, tsk, tsk.” With an unconcerned wave of her wand, Bellatrix sent the improvised projectiles crashing against a wall. “That’s the problem with blood traitor filth like your family. No sense of manners.”

Neville ran to the side, barely avoiding the barrage of curses that Bellatrix effortlessly rained down upon him. The wall behind him exploded, the bricks wrapping and twisting into spikes that threw themselves at him.

Neville slid to the floor, wand moving in a spiral pattern. “Arbor Pullula!” He ignored the feeling of the air displaced by the spikes as they flew above him and focused all his will on the wooden floor at Bellatrix’s feet.

Thick branches sprouted from the floor, constricting her lower half and pulling her down. He did not have time to rejoice, however. With a slash of her wand, Bellatrix summoned a streak of purple flames that burned away her restraints as it swept through the room.

Neville raised his suit’s shield in time to stop it from touching him, but the blue energy crackled and died in contact with the cursed fire.

“You know, I just had a brilliant idea.” Bellatrix stepped away from the burning branches, their wretched forms contorting in the flames as if sucking the very life out of them. “Once I’m done here, I’ll pay a visit to your dear Mum and Dad. Give them a taste of what their son went through for old-time sake. Crucio!”

With no time to think, Neville rolled to the side, ending up far too close form the flames consuming the wall for comfort.

At a disadvantage both by his position and Bellatrix’s momentum, Neville held his ground and faced her spell for spell. Time became a blur as they traded curses and jinxes, ravaging the apartment in their attempts to kill one another. Neither furniture nor dividing walls escaped their zeal, for what the flames did not burn, they blew up and transfigured into deadly traps.

Injured and exhausted, Neville was both mentally and physically spent and did not have much to show for it. Despite his relentless attempts, Bellatrix still stood strong, the mad grin on her face unperturbed by the pain he knew her injured leg must be causing her.

He was not strong enough.

And yet, this was something he would never accept. He had not trained so hard and thought of this day for so long to fail now. His family had suffered so much at her hand. He needed to avenge them. To be the one that finally put her down. To make them proud.

The ceiling came crashing down in a deluge of wood and flames, collapsing the floor under its weight and continuing its fall in the floor under them. Having jumped out of the way in time, Neville and Bellatrix now found themselves on opposite ends of a great chasm, burning debris raining down around them.

“Tsk.” Bellatrix clicked her tongue, a displeased scowl marring her previously joyful expression. “Out of time, it seems. We’ll have to pick this up another day.”

No! She could not get away. Not again.

“Flagrante!”

“Really?” Bellatrix batted away the curse with a sweep of her wand. “I do hope you learn some manners before we meet again. I prefer my toys to be house-broken.”

And with that, she was gone.

“No!” He raged, throwing a curse to the empty space where she had stood a moment ago. “Come back, you coward! Come back and die!”

Neville fell to the floor, his strength spent and his breath painful from taking in too much smoke.

And for what?

Nothing.

He did not have a single thing to show for his efforts. His parent’s tormentor lived to kill and torture another day.

How long until another chance presented itself? How many more would have to die until it all ended?

And what if she had decided to make good on her threat? To go to St Mungo and finish the job?

He could not let that happen.

He got up, wand in hand and ready to apparate away when a great crash echoed nearby as more of the building collapsed, followed by the frightened shrill of a girl from above.

There was still someone in the building.

Despite the flames, the smoke and the ground giving under their feet, someone had survived.

He froze.

He could not let her die.

And yet, staying would give Bellatrix time to exact her vengeance on his parents. No one at St Mungo’s would stand up for them. No one would risk the wrath of Bellatrix Lestrange for a couple of insane patients.

He could not let them die.

With every second of indecision, more of the building came down around him and Bellatrix took one more step toward his Mum and Dad.

Tears filled his eyes, evaporating before they could run down his cheeks as he tightened his grip on his wand.

His father’s wand.

The wand that had been passed down to him with a promise and a hope.

That he would honour their memory.

He could not let them down.

“Erigo Scalae!”

Bricks and planks all around him flew above the chasm, forming makeshift stairs in the air as he climbed them in haste, forcing his gaze upward as he dared not look down.

He heard the cries again, more urgent.

He did not have time to search.

Once on the floor above, he tore through the burning wall with a wave of his wand, revealing a dining room where a small girl was bundled up under a table. She held her head in her hands as she cried, her eyes shut so she would not see the charred hands of her parents coming out of the debris burying the door.

The walls and ceilings groaned, straining under their own weight now that the wall could not support it.

Neville threw himself through the opening, crying out as the flames licked his legs. He fell on the floor near the table, the girl now looking at him.

“Hey there.” His throat was sore, every word painful. “I know it’s scary, but I need you to be brave, ok?” His legs refused to hold his weight, folding under him as he dragged himself to the girl, holding out a hand. “Just... Just take my hand and we’ll get out of here.”

She stayed there, frozen, looking at him with eyes full of fear, her mouth quivering.

The ceiling gave out, coming down upon them.

The girl threw herself at him and Neville twisted in place, apparating them both away.

They reappeared outside, a couple of meters above the road. Neville held the girl tightly against his chest as they fell, the building collapsing in front of them. His head hit the asphalt violently, loosening his grip on the child who rolled over to the side.

The pain in his head and legs flooded his mind, blanking out any coherent thoughts as dark spots filled his vision. Each breath made his burned throat flare with pain and the beating of his heart was the only sound filling his ears.

Maybe it was the concussion, or maybe his mind was trying to ease his end, but despite the agony enveloping his entire body, Neville had never felt so happy. And so he remained, content to lay on the ground, watching the plumes of smoke rise into the sky, feeling his bruised ribs with each laboured breath.

And as the pain recessed and his mind cleared, a great shadow came upon the world.

“What in the hell?”

The first breath Ginny took when she came to was filled with blood and bile, quickly turning it into a painful cough that brought the agony of her entire body to the attention of her addled mind.

Laid out on her back amongst piles of flaming debris, her lower body was pinned down under the remains of one of the buildings bordering the tracks. She tried to push it off, only to let go almost immediately with a strangled cry as pain flared in her right arm. If it was not broken, it was a close thing.

Trapped as she was, she gritted her teeth and looked around, searching the burning remains of the buildings and the derailed train surrounding her in search of her wand.

And that’s when she saw him.

Percy’s mangled body was hanging limply from the train car embedded in a wall, blood pouring out of his wide, unseeing eyes.

She cried out again, tears streaming down her cheeks as she tried to extirpate herself, to push off the rubbles pinning her down and reach him. To hold him and tell him everything that, in her anger, she had kept to herself. To do all she could to bring him back.

To do something. Anything at all.

Because she could not bear the thought of losing him. Of not having been strong enough.

Not again.

And yet, despite her struggle, she remained trapped under the metal and concrete until what little strength she had was spent.

Through the grief, the guilt and the pain plaguing her mind, she knew that she would soon join him if she did not do something. Her survival was already a miracle granted by the reinforced parts of her now ruined armour, but even that had its limits.

With her good arm, she reached for the communication stone embedded in the twisted remains of her armour. One tap on the right runes engraved on its sides was all it would take to call for help.

And yet, she stayed her hand just above it when the light of midday died in the skies above.

Beyond the ruins and the smoke, the sun disappeared and calm blue darkened to black as a starless night fell in mere moments. Out of the darkness, the Moon took its place in the sky, looming upon Britain in its full glory.

For despair could be found on the brightest of days, if one was willing to extinguish the light.

Beasts in the Night

“How about the mountains?“

“No.” Remus did not even look at him, preferring to vanish the month's worth of dust covering everything in the cottage instead.

“Alright... The beach, then!” Sirius was rocking back on the back legs of his chairs, twirling his wand between his fingers as he watched him work. “Far from any town. There’s plenty of those around.”

“Oh yes, and I’d wake up the next morning to find out you drowned trying to plunge off a cliff.” Remus took out a few logs, carefully placing them in the hearth. “I think I’ll pass.”

“You know, you’re no fun when you’re like this.”

Sirius waved his wand nonchalantly, lighting up the fireplace, and put it back in the breast pocket of his jacket. The leathery material it was made of felt strange against his skin, rough in places and far too smooth in others, but he’d be damned if he didn’t wear the first thing his godson had gifted him.

“I don’t really like myself right now, either.”

And for good reasons. His face was pale and tired, the side effects of Wolfsbane already manifesting, despite the early hour of the afternoon. And as the hour passed, he would grow weaker still, the draught sapping his strength until the moon rose and the wolf would be weak enough for Remus to retain his mind after the transformation.

“Yeah, I know.” Sirius sighed. “All I’m saying is that we don’t have to lock ourselves in here every time. I get enough of that the rest of the year already.”

“I’m not going to take any risk, Sirius. You know what happened last time.”

“That doesn’t count. You didn’t have the potion then.”

“And I almost killed you and the others. It only needs to happen once...”

“We’ve been doing this since we were kids. Hell, you even managed on your own for a decade. You need to-"

A series of sharp cracks echoed outside the house. A sound so distinctive any wizard worth their salt would be hard-pressed to misinterpret it.

Sirius brought his chair back to the ground, looking at the door with a frown.

“Waiting for someone?”

“No. No one is even supposed to know we’re here.”

They exchanged a worried look before Sirius approached a window, pushing the thick curtains aside ever so slightly with the tip of his wand. The forest outside was plunged in darkness far too deep for this time of day, even with the century-old trees looming overhead.

“I don’t see—wait, something moved.”

They shivered as something cold and heavy fell upon them, as if someone had draped a blanket that had been left in the snow around them.

“Someone raised wards around the house.” Careful not to pass in front of it, Remus took position on the other side of the window. “We can’t leave.”

“Of course we can’t...” Sirius muttered between clenched teeth. Life had never given them a break and it was not about to start now.

“You’re surrounded, Remus.” An amplified voice easily passed through the thin glass, giving them pause as the all too familiar squeaky tone delivered its ultimatum. “It’s time to come out now.”

Sirius’ hand clenched in a tight fist around his wand and only Remus’ firm grasp on his shoulder stopped him from rushing outside.

“I’m not welcoming visitors today, Peter. How about you go back to whatever hole you crawled from before somebody gets hurt?”

“I don’t want to fight. I just want to talk. To give you a chance to get on the winning side.“

“And grovel at the feet of James and Lily’s killer, like you?” Sirius spat. “You’ve always been a joke Peter, but even I didn’t expect your punchline to be this bad.“

“You should muzzle your dog, Remus, or his bark will get him killed.” Outside, dark silhouettes moved around the trees, too quickly for either of them to sling a curse at or find an opening to flee. “Dumbledore has already lost. Do you really want to fight a lost cause to restore a system that treated you like vermin?”

“When the alternative is working with insane murderers and psychopaths like you and Greyback... I think I’m just fine where I am, thank you.”

“Is that really what you think? We’re the ones fighting for a better world. One where we won’t have to hide from Muggles. Where you can walk down the street without people hiding their children from you. Think about-"

A glimmer of red was their only warning, one that Remus put to good use as he summoned the table against the window before it exploded, shielding them from the worst of it.

“Guess his new friends are as tired of hearing his crap as we are.”

Curses, glass and stones filled the air, the Death Eaters holding nothing back and the last two marauders reciprocating in turn. Sirius stood amidst the chaos, slinging spell after spell with vicious precision, smiling ruefully when he heard the cries of pain of one of their “guests” as they fell.

Without any warning, Remus kicked over a large armchair and dove for cover behind it, dragging Sirius down with him. Not a second later, the far wall of the house exploded, covering them in stone dust.

“What the hell are you doing!”

“You almost caught that with your face!”

“I don’t care!” Sirius barked back right to his face, enraged. “He’s right here! I had him!”

“You won’t have anything if you keep...” A silver gleam reflected in Remus’ eyes and the colour drained from his face. “It can’t-"

His incredulity died as he doubled over, shouting in pain as he pushed Sirius away and out in the open.

Swearing, Sirius hastily put up a shield. It came too late, however, to stop a curse from hitting his left shoulder, scorching his jacket yet leaving him with little more than a dull pain through his arm. He did not have the time to ponder the strange happening, however, as Remus was writhing in pain at his feet, clawing at his clothes as his bones snapped and rearranged themselves in an all too familiar sight.

Sirius dared a look over his shoulder, already knowing the impossible sight that awaited him. The pale moon, shining in its full and horrifying glory through the canopy and the missing wall, half a day before its time.

Too soon. Far too soon.

Rumours of the transformation had spread to the Death Eaters as well, the curses letting place to panicked shouts. Seizing the opportunity, Sirius sliced the air with his wand and the tree from which one of the shouts came from exploded, reigniting the hostilities.

Not keen on waiting for his friend to finish turning, Sirius threw himself out a window, the soft paws of a dog landing on the mossy ground.

He ran through the trees, biting and clawing at the Death Eaters he found, echoing the gruesome spectacle taking place in front of the house.

“Avada-"

“No!”

“Argh!”

His maw full of blood, Padfoot circled back to the house, limping and leaving behind him the body of the last Death Eater hiding in the forest.

In front of the ruined house, Moony had been forced to the ground and Peter was wrestling the wand of one of his henchmen away from him.

“I told you I want him alive!”

“Idiot! You’re gonna get us killed!”

Always happy to help, Padfoot leapt at one of the Death Eaters and bloodied his maw once more. The man let go of his last breath, though not before a Bludgeoning hex sent the dog flying.

“Damn beasts.”

Tossed around like a rag doll among the twigs and stones, Sirius collapsed face down into the moss, his very much human ribs burning painfully. To add insult to injury, the grumbling clouds above finally broke and heavy drops fell upon the forest.

“Remus. It’s me, Peter, remember?” In the distance, Sirius could hear the loathful plea. Trying to drown them in his own shout only produced a growl as pain flared in his lungs. “You wouldn’t harm your friend, would you?”

That little rat.

He dared?

After all he had done?

Fuelled by a rage that dulled his pain, Sirius pushed himself off the ground and onto his elbows, grasping for his wand.

“Please, Remus. I-I just want to help-"

With a feral howl, the Werewolf leapt at Peter, maw open wide and fanged bared.

Green light illuminated the forest and time slowed to a crawl as Sirius saw the last of his friends fall to the ground, like a grotesque puppet whose strings had been cut. There was no trace of the humble and soft-spoken man to be found here, only a rabid beast being put down.

He wanted to shout, to curse at the world and the rat that had ruined his life and all that he loved. No word, however, managed to pass his lips.

He needed to get up. To get to Remus and strangle that damned rat with his own hands. Yet his broken ribs kept him down and forced him to crawl through the mud.

Tearing his gaze from Remus’ remains, Sirius searched for Peter. Nowhere did he find the gloating and satisfaction he had expected, however, for the traitor’s face was twisted in a grimace of shock and despair.

“What have you done!”

“I killed a monster.” The last henchman spat, turning his wand toward Peter. “And you better pray you’re not next for dragging us in this mess in the first pl-"

The threat died on his lips, however. With a scream, barely an incantation, the forest was lit up by emerald light for the second time in as many minutes. As the body of his companion hit the ground, so did Peter’s wand escape his grasp and his legs gave under him, leaving him to fall to his knees before Remus.

He remained there, slumped over the corpse of one who had once called him friend, the silence only broken by the rain hammering his hunched back.

“Peter. Peter!”

Pettigrew barely heard the shouts through the rain, broken up by coughs as they were. Picking up his wand, he turned to see Sirius, dragging himself through the mud to reach him, wand in hand. 

 “You did this! You did all of this!”

Startled, Peter shrank, disappearing from view.

“James ... Lily ... Remus .. You killed them all!”

Sirius peered through the rain, searching for the cowardly rodent until his wand was pried from his hand. A heavy weight came down on his back and he felt the distinctive shape of a wand being pressed against his throat.

“This ... This wasn’t my fault.”

“You brought this on yourself. On all of us!”

“No!” The wand dug deeper into his throat, trembling. “I never wanted things to come to this! I just... I only wanted to talk to him.” Peter’s voice was hoarse and broken up by sobs. His tears disappearing in the rain. “To explain everything. T-to make him understand-”

“What? That you’re a monster? That you betrayed us? I think you clued him in on that a long time ago.”

“I-I needed him to see. I never wanted James and Lily to die. But the Dark Lord ... He’s the only one fighting for us. The only one willing to do what we need to build a world where we wouldn’t have to hide! A world where Remus wouldn’t be treated like a monster.”

“You actually believed that crap?” Sirius couldn’t stop himself. The rueful laugh set his lungs and broken ribs on fire and ended in a coughing fit, but he could not contain it. “You’re insane!.”

“I just ... I wanted my friend back.”

“You killed James and Remus the moment you joined Voldemort. You’re on the same side as the man who bit Remus as a child, Peter!” Sirius roared, struggling against Peter’s hold despite the wand digging painfully into his throat. “You came to “talk” accompanied by Death Eaters! Whatever crap you tell yourself to justify this, you made your choice fifteen years ago.”

“Shut up!” Peter pushed him back down into the mud. “You have no idea what I had to do. What I had to endure while you were fooling around. Remus was the only one that even-”

“Boohoo, sad little Peter had a tough time growing up. Join the club, arsehole!” Sirius spat. “None of us decided to help a dark lord and kill the others because of it! And speaking of which, it looks like you’ll get to finish the set tonight.”

Peter’s hold weakened, allowing him to push him off and free himself. He turned on his back, arms out as he glared at Peter, who towered above him with his wand aimed at his chest.

“Come on. Do it!”

‘’I ... I...”

“Do it! You already took everything from me!”

“I can’t...”

“Do it!” Sirius screamed his throat raw.

“No!” The silver hand came down, no spell coming out of the wand it held. Peter looked down at the last of his friends, his eyes full of pain and his voice broken. “You need to go. Just ... Just leave the country, Sirius. And never look back.”

And with that, he turned and walked away, leaving Sirius behind in the blood-stained mud.

“No.”

Gritting his teeth through the pain, Sirius pushed himself off the ground.

“No!”

Each breath set his lungs on fire, but he did not care.

“You don’t get to walk away. Not again!“

Sirius threw himself at Peter, his form blurring in the air before Padfoot bit his arm, forcing him to drop his wand.

He changed back, pinning him down as he had been a moment ago.

He would not be a coward, however.

Not like Peter.

Never like him.

Beating down Peter’s attempts at shaking him off, Sirius grasped a fistful of hair and a nearby rock.

For James.

For Remus.

With a cry of rage and sorrow, Sirius brought the rock down again and again.

Until the struggle stopped.

Until the pleading stopped.

Until he was the last Marauder.

Finally.

After sixteen years, the traitor was dead and his friends had been avenged.

The moment he had been living for this whole time had passed.

And yet, sitting alone under the rain and surrounded by the bodies of friends and foes alike, he could not feel the joy he had expected.

As he dragged himself to Remus and looked into the yellow eyes of his last friend, he could find no comfort in his presence.

In the distance, the Rochester Cathedral rang the first hour of the afternoon as the full moon shone above. A starless night had fallen over the country, bringing with it a chilling wind.

And yet, despite it all, the Muggles went on with their lives. The only difference was the unusually high number of people who had turned in their radios and tellies to hear experts fail to explain the strange sky and the catastrophes happening across in the country.

All of them blissfully unaware of the beasts lurking in their streets.

On the other shore of the Medway, a beast bared its fangs as it jumped onto the next roof, ready to pierce skin and muscles to satisfy the whispers of its curse.

It had been so long since it had indulged them, their sweet promises coming to it every night despite the lack of prey. Banished to the forests, far from Wizards and Muggles alike, condemned to live in shame of who it was.

But no more.

They had tried to trap them, to herd them like cattle, far away from their prey. They had underestimated them, thinking they faced mindless beasts. And now they would pay the price.

The pack had split, chasing the three little wizards through the streets after their plan had failed.

It could hear her run, her panicked steps echoing in the street below as she vainly tried to escape.

It could smell the metal and magic she had encased herself in, foolishly thinking it would protect her from its fangs and claws.

He could see her waver, her strength waning, allowing the pack to close in on her, prowling on the roofs and alleys.

They ran and ran, never stopping, never resting.

Never standing a chance.

The beast leapt from the roof, tackling its prey. The girl cried out, flailing around as she futilely tried to push the mass of muscles and fur off of her.

Jaws open wide, it plunged for the bite ... Only for its fangs to rip on the metal hidden under the clothes. Growling in rage, the beast bit and clawed at the prey repeatedly, scratching the armour yet never finding purchase in the flesh.

Something hit the beast in the back, throwing it off the girl with a howl of pain echoed by the others as a group of witches and wizards descended upon them.

Standing tall among them, a woman with faded red hair and a battered Auror cloak looked at the beast with cold anger shining in her eyes.

This was a face well-known by the beast, one of the main culprits responsible for the tightening laws against its kind. The very laws that had turned them into outcasts, living from scraps in the darkest reaches of the magical world.

And with a flash of red, her name was the last thing the Werewolf ever knew.

The iron fist of the Ministry.

Amelia Bones.

“Spread out and clean up. There are bound to be more lurking around.”

The last Werewolf fell on the pavement, its burning fur spreading a foul smell that would have turned the stomach of anyone. Fortunately for Amelia, her Aurors were not anyone. They were the best of the best, trained by veterans and kept sharps even when the rest of the country had been content to leave the war behind after He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named had disappeared.

Already, Robards was barking orders and the dozen men they had brought busied themselves, masking any trace of the Werewolves’ presence and apparating up to the roofs to locate the rest of the pack.

Among the bustling street and Aurors running left and right, Amelia stood still, towering over the armoured girl with her arms crossed.

“And what am I going to do with you?”

She could not be older than Susan and here she was, trembling like a leaf as she picked herself up, the smooth metal helmet doing nothing to hide the shock and fear that grasped at her heart.
